# MiniMax-M2.7 Mixed CUDA+ROCm Optimization Status

Date: 2026-06-06

## Benchmark Policy Update

As of 2026-06-06, promoted results must be cache-aware OpenCode-style coding-session benchmarks, not cold one-shot prompt benchmarks.

Primary benchmark requirements:

- One long-lived `llama-server` process, preferably `-np 1`.
- `cache_prompt` enabled.
- Repeated follow-up coding turns with a large shared prefix and smaller changed suffixes.
- Session grows toward the `69376` context limit or otherwise meaningfully stresses long-context behavior.
- Reuse must be proven from response/API/log evidence such as `timings.cache_n`, `tokens_cached`, `/slots`, LCP/f_keep logs, prompt-cache save/load logs, or context-depth counters.
- Cold one-shot PP can remain as diagnostic/reference data only and must not be mixed with cache-aware session conclusions.

Primary benchmark script:

```text
/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-minimax-cache-session.sh
```

The script uses the current best mixed configuration, a single long-lived server, `cache_prompt:true`, and a configurable `PP_STOP_CUTOFF` defaulting to `300` processed prompt tokens/s. This cutoff was added because OpenCode-style use should not continue if the processed prompt path falls below the user's minimum workable threshold.

The script also exposes `BATCH`, `UBATCH`, `PLACEMENT_POLICY`, `DEVICE_SPEED`, `LAYER_SPLIT`, and `OUTPUT_DEVICE` environment overrides so experimental runs can switch between auto graph placement and exact manual splits without editing the script.

## Cache-Aware Coding-Session Baseline

Current status: no promoted cache-aware baseline yet.

First run of the current best mixed configuration:

| run | turn | context depth | cache_n | processed prompt_n | cache ratio | processed PP | effective context PP | TG | status |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-20260606T003539Z` | 1 | 34450 | 0 | 34354 | 0.000 | 334.4944 | 334.4944 | 17.7698 | cold setup, diagnostic |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-20260606T003539Z` | 2 | 45811 | 34449 | 11266 | 0.754 | 200.0801 | 811.8821 | 14.7672 | stopped: processed PP below 300 cutoff |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-ls13137111117-ub800-20260607T035800Z` | 1 | 34450 | 0 | 34354 | 0.000 | 334.3276 | 334.3276 | 17.8378 | cold setup, diagnostic |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-ls13137111117-ub800-20260607T035800Z` | 2 | 45811 | 34449 | 11266 | 0.754 | 200.5461 | 813.7729 | 14.4583 | exact manual `13,13,7,11,11,7` split; stopped below 300 cutoff |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-graph-ub800-20260607T040100Z` | 1 | 34450 | 0 | 34354 | 0.000 | 333.5311 | 333.5311 | 17.7884 | cold setup, diagnostic |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-graph-ub800-20260607T040100Z` | 2 | 45811 | 34449 | 11266 | 0.754 | 199.3829 | 809.0528 | 14.5173 | exact auto-graph rerun of the cold-best `ub800` q4-direct path; stopped below 300 cutoff |

Interpretation:

- Prompt-cache reuse was real on turn 2: response `timings.cache_n = 34449`, `prompt_n = 11266`, and `tokens_cached = 45810`.
- The cached-effective context throughput is high (`811.88 context tokens/s`), but the newly processed suffix throughput is only `200.08 PP`, below the new stop threshold and far below the desired `>=500 PP` OpenCode floor.
- This run is diagnostic only. It does not replace the promoted configuration because the new benchmark gate failed.
- Post-completion `/slots` is not sufficient by itself for cache evidence in this run because the slot showed `n_prompt_tokens_cache = 0` after release while the response timing object correctly recorded `cache_n = 34449`.
- The cold-best `ub800` q4-direct family does not become a cache-aware winner when rerun cleanly. Both the exact manual `13,13,7,11,11,7` split and the exact auto-graph rerun land in the same `~199-201 PP` cached-turn class, so this short-path benchmark branch is closed.

Rejected high-upside scheduler smoke under the same cache-aware gate:

| run | turn | context depth | cache_n | processed prompt_n | cache ratio | processed PP | effective context PP | TG | status |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-single-sched-interleave-cut3-20260606T004724Z` | 1 | 34450 | 0 | 34354 | 0.000 | 332.9196 | 332.9196 | 17.7590 | cold setup, diagnostic |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-single-sched-interleave-cut3-20260606T004724Z` | 2 | 45811 | 34449 | 11266 | 0.754 | 199.8686 | 811.0238 | 14.8699 | stopped: processed PP below 300 cutoff |

Interpretation:

- `LLAMA_PIPELINE_SINGLE_SCHED_INTERLEAVE=3` was active and the server logged `EXPERIMENTAL interleaving prompt ubatches on one scheduler, cut=3`.
- The run did not beat the previous current-best cache-aware baseline. Cold turn PP was slightly lower (`332.92` vs `334.49`), and the cached follow-up turn remained below the cutoff (`199.87` vs `200.08`).
- This specific single-scheduler interleave variant is rejected. It does not provide the desired `>=25%` processed-PP gain and should not receive more tuning unless the executor design changes materially.

This is still an incremental same-shape gain, not the deep pipeline solution. `ub832` now reaches the next ceiling: CUDA3 `MUL_MAT`/cuBLAS scratch OOM.

Command:

```bash
export HSA_OVERRIDE_GFX_VERSION=9.0.6
export ROCBLAS_LAYER=0
export ROCBLAS_LOG_LEVEL=0
export ROCBLAS_TENSILE_LIBPATH=/opt/rocm-custom/lib/rocblas/library
export LD_LIBRARY_PATH=/opt/rocm-custom/lib:/opt/rocm/lib:/opt/rocm/lib64:${LD_LIBRARY_PATH:-}
export PATH=/opt/rocm/bin:${PATH:-}

/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/build-cuda-hip-dl-gfx906/bin/llama-server \
  -m /home/stefan/.lmstudio/models/unsloth/MiniMax-M2.7-GGUF/MiniMax-M2.7-UD-Q4_K_S-00001-of-00004.gguf \
  -c 69376 -ngl 999 -sm layer \
  -dev ROCm1,ROCm0,CUDA3,CUDA1,CUDA0,CUDA2 \
  -fa on -np 1 -fit off --numa distribute --no-warmup --jinja \
  -t 24 -tb 48 -lv 3 -ctk q4_0 -ctv q4_0 \
  -b 448 -ub 448 \
  --placement-policy graph \
  --device-speed 0.55,0.55,1.0,1.0,1.0,1.0 \
  --cuda-fattn-no-stream-k \
  --cuda-fattn-vec-qkv-headroom-mib 0
```

New highest benchmark-prompt candidate replaces the batch flags and adds:

```bash
-b 800 -ub 800
--reserve-pp-outputs 1
--cuda-fattn-mma-q4-0-direct
--cuda-fattn-mma-q4-0-direct-mode all
```

The current `ub800` benchmark payload has a final prompt chunk of `Q=321`, so use the narrow HIP final-chunk cap:

```bash
GGML_CUDA_FATTN_TILE_PARALLEL_BACKENDS=hip
GGML_CUDA_FATTN_TILE_PARALLEL_Q_MIN=321
GGML_CUDA_FATTN_TILE_PARALLEL_Q_MAX=321
GGML_CUDA_FATTN_TILE_PARALLEL_BLOCKS=1
```

For prompt-length-portable validation with `ub800`, use `Q_MIN=2,Q_MAX=799` instead of exact `Q=321`.

For the tiny experimental same-shape rotation gain, add:

```bash
LLAMA_PIPELINE_ROTATE_COPIES=1
```

Notes:

- Upstream server readiness was slow on this cold run: model load finished and the server started listening at about `8:17.99`.
- Output was coherent and started with the same benchmark-style answer prefix, but hash differs from the custom fork: `04d2dfba20e5437909bffcb1af83ae6bbfeafd3951e25ba1d179475b6837cf27`.
- The current custom gfx906 best repeated result is `558.64-558.76 PP / 31.25 TG`, so the custom fork is about `2.8x` faster in PP and `1.6x` faster in TG on this exact payload and context.

Baseline rules:

- Use the same MiniMax-M2.7 Q4_K_S GGUF, `-c 69376`, q4 KV (`-ctk q4_0 -ctv q4_0`), same benchmark payload, same ROCm gfx906 environment, same custom rocBLAS library path, and no concurrent GPU work.
- Use upstream/default flags only. Do not use fork-only flags such as `--layer-split`, `--output-device`, `--placement-policy graph`, `--reserve-pp-outputs`, q4-direct CUDA FA flags, MoE reroute flags, or wave scheduler env vars.
- First baseline command shape: `-sm layer -dev ROCm1,ROCm0,CUDA3,CUDA1,CUDA0,CUDA2 -fa on -b 448 -ub 448`. Completed as the baseline above.
- If upstream starts cleanly, run one default placement baseline and one upstream-supported `-ts` approximation such as `-ts 14,12,7,11,11,7` or `-ts 13,13,7,11,11,7`, then record PP/TG/hash and layer placement logs.
- If upstream cannot build or run mixed CUDA+ROCm in one binary, record that as an upstream blocker and compare against the clean CUDA-only or ROCm-only baseline that does run.

After that baseline, use the fresh upstream tree for a clean custom fork guided by `/home/stefan/plan-cuda+8channelram.md`. That plan is not a MiniMax-only patch: it proposes a generic MoE execution planner for `GGML_OP_MUL_MAT_ID` / routed experts, with MoE profiling, adaptive PP offload thresholds, compact expert staging/cache slots, PP-vs-TG cache separation, expert-parallel activation dispatch, dynamic ubatch, pinned staging pools, and concurrent CPU/GPU expert execution.

This is different from the already-rejected simple MoE experiments. Rejected work moved whole MoE tensors or one layer across devices and paid cross-device activation/weight movement. The clean-fork MoE-planner track should test whether moving smaller activation buckets to devices that own compact resident experts can beat copying or executing full expert tensors.

MoE profiler patch status:

- Implemented first in `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-upstream-minimax-clean`, then ported default-off to the active gfx906 fork.
- New CLI flag: `--moe-profile` with env alias `LLAMA_ARG_MOE_PROFILE`.
- Plumbing: `common_params -> llama_context_params -> llama_cparams -> ggml_backend_sched_set_moe_profile()`.
- Scheduler hook: default-off profiling in `ggml_backend_sched_compute_splits()` for `GGML_OP_MUL_MAT_ID`.
- Output: one `moe_profile:` line per eval with `mul_mat_id`, expert selections, total/average/max unique experts, max experts, max top-k, max tokens, estimated active expert weight bytes, and full expert weight bytes.
- Verification: clean upstream and active gfx906 `llama-server` targets rebuild successfully; `llama-server --help` shows `--moe-profile`; `git diff --check` is clean. The active-gfx906 rebuild took `10:28.85` because public header changes invalidated CUDA/HIP and llama objects while ccache was still cold (`1.89%` hits); an immediate no-op rebuild took `0.708 s`.
- Runtime profile visibility fix: `GGML_LOG_INFO` from the scheduler was not visible in the server log path, so the explicit `--moe-profile` lines now print at warning level.
- Runtime profile artifact: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-upstream-minimax-clean/bench-results/minimax-upstream-moe-profile-visible-small-20260606T011855Z`.
- Runtime profile result on a 4941-token diagnostic prompt: `383.6787 PP`, above the `300 PP` stop threshold.
- Clean-upstream profile result for full `448`-token prompt ubatches: `183` `MUL_MAT_ID` ops per eval, `655872` expert selections, `256` total experts, top-k `8`, `127.49-173.31` average unique experts per expert matmul, and up to `215/256` unique experts in a single expert matmul.
- Active gfx906 profile smoke artifact: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-moe-profile-smoke-20260606T021823Z`.
- Active gfx906 profile smoke result, `BASE_REPEATS=10 TURN_REPEATS=4 MAX_TURNS=1 N_PREDICT=16 LLAMA_ARG_MOE_PROFILE=1`: stopped by the new gate at `271.6812 PP / 32.5341 TG`. This is diagnostic-only because the profiler synchronizes at every routed expert matmul.
- Active gfx906 full `ub800` prompt chunks in that smoke: `183` `MUL_MAT_ID` ops per eval, `1,171,200` expert selections, `256` total experts, top-k `8`, `218.61-237.87` average unique experts per expert matmul, max `244-256/256` unique experts, estimated active expert weight `~101-110 GiB` versus full expert weight `~115.8 GiB`.
- Added optional shard-load estimates via `GGML_MOE_PROFILE_SHARDS=N` to estimate expert-owner load balance for expert-axis parallelism.
- Active gfx906 shard smoke artifact: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-moe-profile-shards4-smoke-20260606T022520Z`.
- Active gfx906 shard smoke result, `GGML_MOE_PROFILE_SHARDS=4 BASE_REPEATS=4 TURN_REPEATS=2 MAX_TURNS=1 N_PREDICT=8`: `373.1852 PP / 31.1175 TG`, above the `300 PP` stop threshold. The full `ub800` chunk had shard selections `281862,297030,290946,301362`, total selection imbalance `1.029x`, and max per-node shard unique `64/64`. This suggests a 4-CUDA expert-id owner split is load-balanced enough to justify a one-layer expert-axis smoke; the hard blocker is storage/scatter implementation, not router skew.
- Added `--moe-profile-json PATH` for structured routed-MoE profile dumps. The scheduler now writes one JSON file per eval: the base path for eval 1, then `.evalN.json` for later evals.
- Structured-profile verification artifact: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-moe-profile-json-20260607T014020Z`.
- Structured-profile verification result, `GGML_MOE_PROFILE_SHARDS=4 LLAMA_ARG_MOE_PROFILE=1 LLAMA_ARG_MOE_PROFILE_JSON=... BASE_REPEATS=4 TURN_REPEATS=2 MAX_TURNS=1 N_PREDICT=8`: one-turn cache-aware diagnostic completed at `375.4333 PP / 31.8027 TG`. The server log shows `moe_profile_json: wrote ...` for evals 1-10, and the emitted JSON includes top-level shard arrays plus per-layer and per-node expert histograms.
- JSON schema check on `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-moe-profile-json-20260607T014020Z/moe-profile.json.eval2.json`: `62` layers, `186` nodes, `top_experts` arrays on both layers and nodes, and `shard_count=4` with four-entry `shard_selections` / `shard_unique_total`. This is the first artifact in the repo that exposes MiniMax routed-expert traffic in a machine-readable form.
- Added reusable analyzer: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/scripts/analyze-moe-profile.py`.
- Analyzer artifact: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cache-session-moe-profile-json-20260607T014020Z/moe-profile-analysis.txt`.
- Layer-level conclusion from the analyzer:
  - There is no hidden sparse MoE regime in full prompt processing.
  - Full `ub800` prompt eval (`eval2`) still spans `213-255 / 256` unique experts per MoE layer, with median `235`.
  - A repeatable narrower late-layer band exists around layers `25-31` plus `59-60`, but even those layers still touch roughly `71-86%` of all experts.
  - Top-expert concentration remains modest: the meaningful full-PP layers reach only about `9-11%` top-1 share and about `34-38%` top-8 share in the narrowest late-layer band.
  - Top-8 expert overlap between the full `eval2` chunk and the later `eval3` chunk has median Jaccard only `0.333`, so hot experts are not stable enough to justify a simple sparse-residency or hot-expert cache design.
  - Some of those narrower late layers do show real shard-selection skew, up to about `2-3x`, so the only surviving MoE interpretation is better dispatch/load-shaping, not keeping only a small expert subset resident.
- Placement interaction from the same evidence:
  - Under the freed-CUDA one-layer test split `15,13,7,10,10,7`, layers `59-60` are already on `CUDA2`, and only the tail of the narrower `25-31` band (`25-27`) still sits on the ROCm0 bottleneck stage.
  - So the narrower-band evidence by itself does not justify more one-layer retarget sweeps. Most of the apparently nicer MoE layers are not on the slow AMD stages under the tested split.
- Profiler overhead fix: the JSON path originally re-read and synchronized the same `ids_tensor` for every `MUL_MAT_ID` node. The scheduler now reuses the previous ids/expert-hit cache for repeated MoE ops sharing one ids tensor, matching the existing split-copy path and avoiding avoidable profiler distortion.
- Interpretation: MiniMax prompt processing activates experts broadly. Cold-expert CPU offload, simple LRU hot-expert caching, and copying only a few active experts are not high-PP paths. The remaining MoE path with large theoretical upside is activation-bucket expert parallelism with compact resident expert slots, where activations move to expert owners instead of moving whole expert tensors or whole MoE subgraphs.

Expert-axis CUDA split prototype status:

- Implemented default-off in `ggml/src/ggml-cuda/ggml-cuda.cu`.
- Enable with `GGML_CUDA_SPLIT_MUL_MAT_ID=1` and `GGML_CUDA_SPLIT_MUL_MAT_ID_EXPERT_AXIS=1`.
- Uses existing `CUDA*_Split` buffer selection through `--override-tensor` / `LLAMA_ARG_OVERRIDE_TENSOR`.
- Storage change: eligible 3D quantized split-buffer expert tensors are split by expert axis `ne[2]` instead of output-row axis `ne[1]`.
- Execution change: split `MUL_MAT_ID` builds compact selected-token rows for each CUDA expert-owner shard, runs the existing quantized MMQ path per local expert, copies compact results back to the split main CUDA device, and scatters them into the normal `[output, topk, token]` result layout.
- The previous row-split `MUL_MAT_ID` path remains default for non-expert-axis runs.
- Build result after this source-only change: `llama-server` rebuilt successfully in `13.29 s`.

Expert-axis smoke results:

| run | override | split weights | layer split | ubatch | result | status |
|---|---|---|---|---:|---:|---|
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-split-l20-smoke-20260606T023951Z` | `blk.20.ffn_(up|gate|down)_exps.weight=CUDA3_Split` | `1,1,1,1` | `14,12,7,11,11,7` | 800 | CUDA3 compute-buffer OOM at context init | rejected |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-split-l20-cuda0-ub448-smoke-20260606T024042Z` | `blk.20.ffn_(up|gate|down)_exps.weight=CUDA0_Split` | `1,1,1,1` | `14,12,7,11,11,7` | 448 | CUDA3 compute-buffer OOM during pipeline reservation; fallback would disable pipeline | rejected |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-split-l20-cuda0-ub256-smoke-20260606T024126Z` | `blk.20.ffn_(up|gate|down)_exps.weight=CUDA0_Split` | `1,1,1,1` | `14,12,7,11,11,7` | 256 | runtime CUDA3 MMQ OOM in split `MUL_MAT_ID` | rejected |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-split-l20-cuda0-2x3090-ub256-smoke-20260606T024205Z` | `blk.20.ffn_(up|gate|down)_exps.weight=CUDA0_Split` | `1,1,0,0` | `14,12,7,11,11,7` | 256 | CUDA1 compute-buffer OOM during pipeline reservation; fallback would disable pipeline | rejected |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-split-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub256-smoke-20260606T024300Z` | `blk.20.ffn_(up|gate|down)_exps.weight=CUDA0_Split` | `1,1,0,0` | `15,13,7,10,10,7` | 256 | `235.8910 PP` | rejected by `PP_STOP_CUTOFF=300` |

Interpretation:

- The expert-axis code path is functional enough to reach a generation request when CUDA memory is freed.
- It is not a high-PP candidate in the current prototype. To make it load, CUDA layers had to be reduced and ubatch lowered; the resulting first-turn PP was only `235.89`, below the user's hard cutoff and far below the current cold diagnostic best.
- This rejects the simple one-layer expert-axis split/offload form. A future version would need a materially different design: device-side id compaction, persistent per-device activation/output buffers, no per-expert host scans, no CUDA3 scratch blow-up, and enough CUDA headroom without giving layers back to AMD. That is no longer a near-term high-probability path.

Expert-axis follow-up screening:

- The current split-expert path in [ggml-cuda.cu](/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/ggml/src/ggml-cuda/ggml-cuda.cu) originally did host-side bucketing with nested `device x expert x token x topk` scans. That was replaced with a linear two-pass host bucketing path (`tokens_per_expert` plus prefix offsets) to remove the worst host-side `O(expert * token * topk)` loop.
- A second prototype then changed the remote-owner transfer shape so expert-axis owners no longer receive the full `src1` activation tensor. The main CUDA device now builds compact owner-local activation buckets first and peer-copies only those compact buckets to remote owner GPUs. The path still round-trips router ids through host and is still only a one-layer prototype.

Expert-axis follow-up results:

| run | change | ubatch | result | decision |
|---|---|---:|---:|---|
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub256-hostopt-small-20260606T230854Z` | linear host bucketing, same small smoke as prior `ub256` check | 256 | `237.2929 PP` | only about `+0.6%` over the prior `235.8910 PP`; not enough |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub384-hostopt-small-20260606T230951Z` | linear host bucketing, higher-fitting small smoke | 384 | `303.6018 PP` | small-shape gate cleared, worth one full-prompt check |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub384-hostopt-full-20260606T231032Z` | same host-bucketing path on the full prompt; manually stopped once live PP stayed below cutoff | 384 | live PP decayed below `300` by about `18048` processed tokens and reached about `199.01 PP` by `25728` processed tokens | rejected for OpenCode/cache-aware use |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub384-compactxfer-small-20260606T232317Z` | compact remote activation transfer: build owner-local buckets on the main CUDA device, then peer-copy only those compact buckets to remote owners | 384 | `300.1031 PP` | essentially flat/slightly slower than the `303.6018 PP` host-bucketing smoke, so no full-prompt rerun |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub384-deviceids-small-20260606T232927Z` | replace the full routed-id D2H copy and CPU bucketing with CUDA-side `mm_ids_helper`, copying back only `expert_bounds` to host | 384 | `299.9353 PP` | screened out at the small-shape gate; removing the host id path alone is not enough |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub384-batchedmmq-small-20260606T233907Z` | replace the per-expert CPU launch loop with one batched quantized MMQ ids-kernel per owner GPU, reusing the existing `expert_bounds` MMQ backend | 384 | `298.1485 PP` | also screened out; the current one-layer expert-axis override path is no longer worth tuning incrementally |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub384-precompreuse-small-20260606T234948Z` | persistent owner-local q8 reuse for compact activation buckets across the `gate/up` pair, enabled with `GGML_CUDA_MMQ_PRECOMP_REUSE_Q8=1 GGML_CUDA_MMQ_PRECOMP_REUSE_Q8_ALL_DEVICES=1` | 384 | `299.7543 PP` | still below the gate; persistent q8 reuse in the current one-layer split path is not enough |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub384-fusedffn-small-20260607T000709Z`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub384-fusedffnlog-small-20260607T000833Z`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-expert-axis-l20-2x3090-freecuda-ub384-fusedffnlog2-small-20260607T001011Z` | attempted a graph-level split-aware fused expert FFN executor to collapse `gate + up + GLU + down` into one gather/copy and one return/scatter | 384 | `298.3125 PP`, `297.6023 PP`, `299.5445 PP` | screened out; the fusion never logged as matched on the live MiniMax one-layer override graph, so this became a graph-variant project rather than a fast high-confidence PP path |

Interpretation of the follow-up screening:

- Host-loop cleanup helped only marginally. It did not change the full-prompt outcome enough to keep this branch active as a practical OpenCode path.
- Compact remote activation transfer is directionally the right data-movement shape, but changing that one piece in a one-layer prototype is still not enough to produce a meaningful PP jump.
- Device-side id compaction and even the batched quantized MMQ ids-kernel are still not enough when grafted onto the current one-layer override path. That strongly suggests the remaining bottleneck is the overall one-layer prototype shape itself: extra gather/copy/scatter boundaries, temporary compact buffers, and lack of multi-layer resident expert ownership.
- Persistent owner-local q8 reuse across the `gate/up` pair also failed to move the one-layer split path above the smoke gate. This screens out the last obvious “reuse the same compact activation twice” optimization inside the current override structure.
- A graph-level split-aware fused expert FFN attempt also failed the taste screen. Three small-smoke runs stayed below `300 PP`, and trace-enabled reruns never showed the fusion matching the live MiniMax override graph. That means the real graph shape for this layer likely includes additional per-expert bias/scale variants or other layout details, so pursuing it further would be a larger graph-pattern project rather than a quick PP lever.
- This means further partial tuning of the current one-layer expert-axis prototype is not justified. The only remaining MoE/expert path with believable large upside is a deeper CUDA-only activation-bucket executor with compact resident expert tensors/slots, device-side id compaction, persistent per-owner buffers, and RAM only as overflow.

## Mixed Tensor / Near-P2P Track

Goal: test whether the existing custom host-staged mixed-vendor copy bridge can make AMD+NVIDIA tensor-mode useful for MiniMax at the production shape (`Q4_K_S` model, q4 KV, `n_ctx=69376`).

Bridge status before this stage:

- True AMD/NVIDIA GPU P2P is not exposed on this host.
- The fork has a custom mixed-vendor copy path controlled by `GGML_MIXED_VENDOR_COPY=1`, `GGML_MIXED_VENDOR_COPY_CHUNK_BYTES`, and `GGML_MIXED_VENDOR_COPY_BUFFERS`.
- Earlier small-model tensor-mode tests worked but were much slower than single-device/layer-mode because per-token collectives/meta overhead dominated.

Tensor smoke tooling:

- Script: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-minimax-tensor-smoke.sh`.
- Updated to expose `CACHE_K` and `CACHE_V` so q4-KV tensor-mode can be tested directly instead of hard-coding f16 KV.

Full-context q4-KV tensor placement results:

| run | device order | tensor split | result |
|---|---|---|---|
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-fullctx-smoke-20260606T024501Z` | `CUDA0,CUDA1,CUDA2,CUDA3,ROCm0,ROCm1` | `33,33,17,17,48,52` | model tensor allocation OOM on CUDA2 (`17417.68 MiB` planned on 16 GB card) |
| multiple `minimax-tensor-plan-*` plan-only sweeps | CUDA-first and layer-mode mixed order | many integer/fractional splits | tensor placement is coarse/discontinuous; many splits overfill one 16 GB CUDA card or ROCm1 |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-fullctx-ts21-21-11-11-31-31-smoke-20260606T025040Z` | `CUDA0,CUDA1,CUDA2,CUDA3,ROCm0,ROCm1` | `21,21,11,11,31,31` | model tensors fit, then context init rejects q4 KV with `SPLIT_MODE_TENSOR`: `simultaneous use ... not implemented` |

Code changes added for diagnosis:

- `LLAMA_UNSAFE_ALLOW_TENSOR_SPLIT_QUANT_KV=1` in `src/llama-context.cpp` bypasses the hard q4-KV tensor-mode rejection with a warning.
- `LLAMA_TENSOR_SPLIT_KV=...` in `src/llama-model.cpp` applies an env-only tensor split override to `cache_k_l*` / `cache_v_l*` tensors. This lets KV cache placement differ from model-weight placement.
- `LLAMA_TENSOR_SPLIT_ATTN=...` in `src/llama-model.cpp` applies an env-only tensor split override to attention tensors and KV cache together. This is a diagnostic alternative to separate KV-only split: it keeps K/V update tensors and cache tensors partition-compatible while leaving the FFN/model-weight split unchanged.
- `GGML_META_MINIMAX_PRE_RESHAPE_QK_NORM=1` in `src/models/minimax-m2.cpp` is a default-off diagnostic that reshapes Q/K into head form before distributed Q/K RMS norm, so the meta backend sees the head axis earlier.
- `GGML_META_UNSAFE_RESHAPE_HEAD_TOKEN_SPLIT=1` in `ggml/src/ggml-backend-meta.cpp` is a default-off diagnostic remap for flattened head/token reshape split states. It is evidence-gathering only, not a production correctness fix.
- `GGML_META_UNSAFE_RESHAPE_AXIS0_RATIO_SPLIT=1` in `ggml/src/ggml-backend-meta.cpp` is a default-off diagnostic remap for reshape cases that flatten a split head/token axis into destination axis 0.
- `GGML_META_UNSAFE_VIEW_MERGE01_SPLIT=1` in `ggml/src/ggml-backend-meta.cpp` is a default-off diagnostic remap for KV write views that merge dims 0 and 1 into the row axis before `SET_ROWS`.
- `GGML_META_DEBUG_FLASH_ATTN=1` in `ggml/src/ggml-backend-meta.cpp` is a default-off diagnostic that dumps Flash Attention source split axes before the Meta handler asserts.
- `GGML_META_DEBUG_SET_ROWS=1` in `ggml/src/ggml-backend-meta.cpp` is a default-off diagnostic that dumps source/destination split states before the `SET_ROWS` compatibility assertion.
- `GGML_META_ALLOC_TENSOR_LOG_MIB=N` in `ggml/src/ggml-backend-meta.cpp` is a default-off allocation attribution diagnostic that prints large per-simple-device tensors during Meta allocation planning.

Unsafe q4-KV tensor smoke results:

| run | model split | KV split | extra env | result |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-unsafe-ts21-21-11-11-31-31-ub256-20260606T025230Z` | `21,21,11,11,31,31` | same as model | `LLAMA_UNSAFE_ALLOW_TENSOR_SPLIT_QUANT_KV=1` | model tensors fit; q4 KV OOM on ROCm1 (`1086.15 MiB`) because model placement left too little headroom |

| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-prereshape-20260606T031549Z` | `21,21,11,11,31,31` | `30,30,15,10,30,5` | plus `GGML_META_MINIMAX_PRE_RESHAPE_QK_NORM=1` | still fails at the same reshape, showing pre-reshape Q/K norm alone is not enough |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-prereshape-headsplit-20260606T031754Z` | `21,21,11,11,31,31` | `30,30,15,10,30,5` | plus unsafe head/token reshape remap | moves past the first Q reshape, then hits K reshape: source `[64,32,1,1]` to destination `[128,8,2,1]` |

| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-setrows-debug-20260606T053241Z` | `21,21,11,11,31,31` | `30,30,15,10,30,5` | plus `GGML_META_DEBUG_SET_ROWS=1` | confirms the `SET_ROWS` blocker: `k_cur` source is split axis 0 as `[128,128,128,128,256,256]` while `cache_k_l0` destination is split axis 0 as `[256,256,128,0,256,128]`; separate KV split fixes memory but makes KV writes partition-incompatible |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-samesplit-allocdetail-20260606T053805Z`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-samesplit-allocdetail64-20260606T053836Z` | `21,21,11,11,31,31` | same as model | `GGML_META_ALLOC_TENSOR_LOG_MIB=256/64` | allocation attribution shows same-split model placement leaves ROCm1 at `31497.13 MiB` before KV; q4 KV needs another `1086.15 MiB` there and OOMs. Large ROCm1 weight pressure is distributed across many expert tensors, not one removable tensor |
| `minimax-tensor-q4kv-samesplit-autoplan-*` capped search, 90 candidates | many nearby same-split candidates around `21,21,11,11,31,31` | same as model | plan-only q4-KV tensor placement search | found `0` plausible same-split candidates with enough ROCm1 and CUDA headroom; `-ts` tuning alone did not unlock production q4-KV tensor mode |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-attnsplit-axis0narrow-20260606T055639Z` | `21,21,11,11,31,31` | attention+KV split `30,30,15,10,30,5` via `LLAMA_TENSOR_SPLIT_ATTN` | distributed Q/K RMS norm, unsafe head/token reshape, unsafe axis0 reshape | server reaches ready at `n_ctx=69376` and q4 KV; tiny 12-token prompt runs at `23.27 PP / 3.27 TG`. This proves the production-shape q4-KV graph can be made executable, but the tiny prompt is not a performance result |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-attnsplit-prompt32-ub256-20260606T055756Z`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-attnsplit-prompt32-setrowsdebug-20260606T055919Z` | `21,21,11,11,31,31` | attention+KV split `30,30,15,10,30,5` | first larger prompt attempt | server starts, but 961-token prompt crashes at `SET_ROWS` because a KV write view keeps source split axis 1 instead of the merged row axis |
| `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-tensor-q4kv-attnsplit-viewmerge2-prompt32-20260606T060353Z` | `21,21,11,11,31,31` | attention+KV split `30,30,15,10,30,5` | plus unsafe view merge01 remap | graph-functional production-shape q4-KV tensor mode on a 961-token prompt, but only `203.10 PP / 6.60 TG`; rejected by the user’s `300 PP` minimum and far below layer mode |

Interpretation:

- Mixed AMD+NVIDIA tensor-mode at full context is now graph-functional for a small production-shape q4-KV smoke, but not performance-viable in the current design.
- The previous hard q4-KV rejection was only the first blocker. After bypassing it, separate KV split was required to avoid ROCm1 OOM.
- After memory was fixed, the meta backend still could not propagate MiniMax tensor splits through q/k norm, head/token reshapes, and `SET_ROWS` graph shapes.
- The `SET_ROWS` debug run proves this is not only a conservative assertion: with separate model/KV splits, the current K/V update source shard and destination cache shard describe different token/head partitions. The Meta backend currently has allreduce support for partial sums, but it does not have an all-gather/repartition primitive for cross-partition KV writes.
- A capped same-split placement search found no viable q4-KV fit, so there is no current `-ts`-only workaround for production tensor mode at `n_ctx=69376`.
- The `LLAMA_TENSOR_SPLIT_ATTN` diagnostic keeps attention and KV partitions compatible enough to run, but the current mixed tensor path reaches only `203.10 PP` on a 961-token prompt and only `6.60 TG`.
- This confirms P2P/tensor is a real stage, but the current direct mixed AMD+NVIDIA tensor mode is not a high-PP path. It loses to layer mode before even reaching cache-aware OpenCode benchmarking.
- Near-term high-PP implication: close direct mixed-vendor tensor mode for the current work cycle. If revisited later, the next code target is not transport bandwidth; it is a materially different hybrid design or real split-state/repartition support that can avoid per-layer mixed-vendor collectives and still keep K/V source/cache partitions compatible.

## Promoted PP Reservation Validation

The `--reserve-pp-outputs 1` candidate was validated beyond the original benchmark prompt. Clean validations show a consistent PP gain from larger `ub512`; two prompt designs are rejected as quality checks because they trigger prompt echo or immediate EOS behavior.

Superseded conclusion: `--reserve-pp-outputs 1 -b 512 -ub 512` was the first practical larger-ubatch candidate. It is now superseded by the `ub557` HIP irregular-chunk cap family on the original benchmark and on the accepted `alt_a`/`alt_d` validation prompts. Any final production recommendation should still keep output-sanity checks in the benchmark loop because larger ubatches change numerical trajectory.

Updated validation shows the `ub768` family improves the accepted validation prompts too. The original benchmark payload ends with a `Q=1` final chunk, so the fastest original-payload command needs no cap. The generalized `Q_MIN=2,Q_MAX=767` cap is the portable form because final prompt chunk size changes with prompt length.

| payload | previous accepted `ub512` PP / TG | `ub768` PP / TG | quality status | artifact |
|---|---:|---:|---|---|
| original benchmark | `487.5332 / 31.0895` | `546.0391 / 31.3499`, repeat `546.7421 / 30.2602` | accepted, coherent | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-ub768-nocap-20260605T052238Z`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-ub768-nocap-repeat-20260605T052333Z` |
| `alt_a` engineering validation | `431.2367 / 28.8579` | `502.5756 / 29.9424` | accepted, coherent | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-ub768-irregular-validate-alt_a-20260605T052750Z` |
| `alt_d` benchmark-style validation | `461.6668 / 30.6250` | `536.7050 / 31.5158` | accepted, coherent | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-ub768-irregular-validate-alt_d-20260605T052853Z` |

| shifted split + layer-0 MoE weights/ops on CUDA1, `-b 448 -ub 448` | 379.4461 | 29.5613 | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-moe-weight-override-20260604T043441Z` |
| MoE top-k profile run, `n_predict=1` | 346.8946 | n/a | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-moe-profile-20260604T032751Z` |
| CPU router projection probe | 335.0743 | 24.7011 | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cpu-gating-probe-20260604T021246Z` |

## Qwen3-Coder-Next CUDA-only comparison

This comparison uses the same prompt payload shape, `-c 69376`, `-ctk q8_0 -ctv q8_0`, `-b 512 -ub 512`, `--reserve-pp-outputs 1`, and only the four NVIDIA GPUs (`CUDA0,CUDA2,CUDA1,CUDA3`). It is not directly comparable to MiniMax model quality or architecture, but it shows what the CUDA cards can do without the mixed CUDA+ROCm layer pipeline bottleneck.

| model/config | residency | PP tokens/s | TG tokens/s | prompt tokens | output tokens | artifact |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Qwen3-Coder-Next `UD-Q8_K_XL`, Q8 KV, fallback `-ngl 44`, CPU output | 43 CUDA layers, 5 CPU layers, CPU output | 421.7053 | 15.7392 | 11521 | 128 | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/qwen3-coder-next-cuda-q8kv-partial-20260605T014650Z` |
| Qwen3-Coder-Next `UD-Q5_K_XL`, Q8 KV, cold first run `-ngl 999`, GPU output | all 48 layers on CUDA, CUDA3 output | 158.0469 | 21.0136 | 11521 | 128 | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/qwen3-coder-next-cuda-q5-q8kv-20260605T030248Z` |
| Qwen3-Coder-Next `UD-Q5_K_XL`, Q8 KV, hot repeat `-ngl 999`, GPU output | all 48 layers on CUDA, CUDA3 output | 2673.6441 | 85.8011 | 11521 | 128 | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/qwen3-coder-next-cuda-q5-q8kv-repeat-20260605T030540Z` |
| Qwen3-Coder-Next `UD-Q5_K_XL`, Q8 KV, user-confirmed downloaded model, `-ngl 999`, GPU output | all 48 layers on CUDA, CUDA3 output | 2659.3504 | 87.0754 | 11521 | 128 | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/qwen3-coder-next-cuda-q5-q8kv-user-full-20260605T032837Z` |

The Q5 first run is not a steady-state number: after the CUDA architecture rebuild, the first prompt chunk paid cold kernel/JIT/cache overhead and reported only `158 PP`. The immediate repeat used the same output hash (`0591778c...`) and reached `2673.64 PP / 85.80 TG`. The user-confirmed downloaded-model run also used the same output hash and reached `2659.35 PP / 87.08 TG`. The repeat logs confirm full CUDA residency with no CPU layers: CUDA layer split `15,10,14,9`, output on `CUDA3`, CPU layers `0`.

## Accepted code changes

- Exact manual layer placement: `--layer-split`.
- Output tensor override: `--output-device`.
- Auto placement policies: `memory`, `max-cuda`, `balanced`, `graph`.
- Placement summary logging with per-device layer count, weights, KV estimate, free VRAM, and backend.
- CUDA FA diagnostic and tuning flags:
  - `--cuda-fattn-no-stream-k`
  - `--cuda-fattn-vec-qkv-devices`
  - `--cuda-fattn-vec-backends` (diagnostic backend filter for vector forcing: `cuda`, `hip`, or `all`)
  - `--cuda-fattn-vec-qkv-kctx-min`
  - `--cuda-fattn-vec-q-min`
  - `--cuda-fattn-vec-q-max`
  - `--cuda-fattn-vec-qkv-headroom-mib`
  - `--cuda-fattn-vec-tmp-headroom-mib` (diagnostic/stability, not a winning setting)
  - `--cuda-fattn-vec-nthreads` (diagnostic/tuning, not a winning setting)
  - `--cuda-fattn-mma-q4-0-direct` (experimental q4_0 direct-dequant MMA FA; not accepted as winning)
  - `--cuda-fattn-mma-q4-0-direct-q-min`
  - `--cuda-fattn-mma-q4-0-direct-q-max`
  - `--cuda-fattn-mma-q4-0-direct-kctx-min`
  - `--cuda-fattn-mma-q4-0-direct-kctx-max`
  - `GGML_CUDA_FATTN_VEC_MAX_PARALLEL_BLOCKS` (diagnostic, not a winning setting)
- CUDA MMQ diagnostic flags:
  - `--cuda-mmq-no-stream-k` (rejected for performance)
  - `--cuda-mmq-force-x`
  - `--cuda-mmq-disable-devices`
- MiniMax MoE reroute diagnostic flags:
  - `--minimax-moe-device`
  - `--minimax-moe-layers`
- CUDA MoE router histogram diagnostics:
  - `GGML_CUDA_MOE_PROFILE=1`
  - `GGML_CUDA_MOE_PROFILE_MIN_ROWS=N`
  - `GGML_CUDA_MOE_PROFILE_MAX_CALLS=N`
- Scheduler profiling diagnostics:
  - `--profile-splits`
  - `--profile-nodes`
  - `GGML_SCHED_PROFILE_COPY_DETAIL=1` for per-input split-copy wait/dispatch logging when `GGML_SCHED_PROFILE_COPY=1` is enabled.
  - `LLAMA_PIPELINE_RANGE_EXEC=1` for the default-off split-range scheduler smoke path. This calls the new range API over the full split list and is behavior-preserving at `555.4306 PP / 30.2871 TG` on the current `ub800` best shape.
- Prompt-processing output-row reservation:
  - `--reserve-pp-outputs N`
  - `LLAMA_ARG_RESERVE_PP_OUTPUTS=N`
  - `LLAMA_RESERVE_PP_OUTPUTS=N` (direct diagnostic override retained; default behavior is unchanged)
- MiniMax tensor-mode diagnostics/prototype:
  - `GGML_META_UNSAFE_LOCAL_AXIS0_RMS_NORM=1` lets axis-0 `RMS_NORM` run locally for smoke testing only; this is mathematically wrong and not a production path.
  - `GGML_META_MINIMAX_SPLIT_QK_NORM=1` shards MiniMax `attn_q_norm`/`attn_k_norm` weights to match tensor-mode Q/K projection shards.
  - `GGML_META_MINIMAX_DISTRIBUTED_RMS_NORM=1` decomposes MiniMax Q/K projection RMS norms into local `SQR`, `SUM_ROWS`, meta allreduce of row sums, and local normalization. This is the first correct f16-KV tensor-mode graph path, but it is not a PP win.
  - `LLAMA_HYBRID_CUDA_META=1` collapses selected CUDA devices into a CUDA-only Meta layer-stage while preserving ROCm devices as normal layer-mode stages. It is diagnostic/prototype only; f16-KV runs but loses to normal layer mode. Q4 KV now runs with the newer unsafe Meta reshape/view remaps, but full-context cache-aware throughput is below the `300 PP` stop gate.

## Rejected or non-winning probes

- Moving output to crowded 3090s caused pipeline fallback or startup OOM.
- Reduced-CUDA layer splits could run higher ubatch, but PP fell below the best graph policy result.
- Global q4 direct-vector FA avoided OOM but was much slower.
- CUDA3-only vector fallback is useful, but the automatic FA memory guard now wins over the fixed CUDA3/kctx threshold.
- Auto FA guard headrooms above `0` MiB did not improve PP in the low-headroom sweep; `128` and `256` MiB were clean but slightly slower.
- Re-enabling stream-K with the auto FA guard produced one slightly faster run (`474.67 PP`) but the repeat fell to `473.11 PP`, so no-stream-K remains the safer recommendation.
- Higher ubatch on the graph split did not win: `ub452/456/464` OOM during completion, `ub480` failed startup, and `ub512` fell back without pipeline parallelism and dropped to `393.19 PP`.
- Disabling the automatic quantized-KV vector fallback at `ub448` caused CUDA OOM during the request, proving the fallback is required for the current best high-context run.
- Capping vector FA parallel blocks proves the fallback combine buffer is a memory pressure source, but it is slower: the best vector-only cap probe was `451.32 PP`.
- Global FA `MAX_PARALLEL_BLOCKS` caps are rejected. The older cap sweep only reached `448.91 PP / 21.49 TG` for `ub452 cap1`, while larger caps/ubatches OOMed or failed; a later `ub528 cap1` probe was aborted as non-competitive with no completed result.
- Auto-capping vector FA temp parallelism confirms the same bottleneck. It made the previously failing `ub452` run complete, but the best result was only `453.10 PP`; `ub456` still failed during the request. Debug logs show CUDA3 clamping vector FA from `parallel_blocks 2 -> 1` with only about `5-7 MiB` free.
- Increasing vector FA to 256 threads per block was not a win. It tied the best at `ub448` within noise (`474.15 PP`) but did not beat it; `ub452` completed at only `452.22 PP`, and `ub456` still failed.
- Moving one or two layers from the 5070 Ti cards to AMD makes `ub512` stable, but the extra AMD stage work cancels the ubatch gain. Best AMD-shift split was `14,13,6,11,11,7` at `469.20 PP`.
- Reducing AMD from `13+13` layers to `12+12` with exact split `12,12,7,12,12,7` is blocked by 3090 weight residency. With `--placement-policy memory --layer-split 12,12,7,12,12,7`, each 12-layer 3090 buffer needs `23900.12 MiB`, while CUDA0/CUDA1 report only `23857 MiB` free; CUDA0 allocation fails before KV or compute buffers. This means one extra full layer per 3090 misses by only about `43 MiB`, making surgical partial-tensor offload a plausible next lead.
- Surgical CPU attention offload can reduce the 12-layer 3090 buffer but does not leave enough margin. Moving `blk.31` and `blk.43` attention weights to CPU reduced each 3090 buffer to `23855.50 MiB`, but `cudaMalloc` still failed; moving two attention layers per 3090 group reduced weights to `23810.87 MiB` but then failed allocating the `914.62 MiB` CUDA0 KV buffer.
- CPU offload of the extra layer MoE experts proves the `12,12,7,12,12,7` memory shape can load, but it is not viable: `blk.31` and `blk.43` `ffn_*_exps.weight=CPU` ran at only `335.08 PP / 28.52 TG` and produced prompt-echo hash `5b712df...`.
- Partial CPU offload of only the extra layer `ffn_gate_exps` and `ffn_up_exps` tensors is also not viable. It ran at `354.07 PP / 29.09 TG` with hash `242ba0...`, far below the current `~487 PP` baseline, in `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cuda-heavy-extra-moe-cpu-gate-up-31-43-20260605T032528Z`.
- Ordinary CUDA-to-CUDA offload of the same extra-layer `ffn_gate_exps` and `ffn_up_exps` tensors does not fit on the 5070s with the current output placement. `blk.31 -> CUDA3` and `blk.43 -> CUDA2` failed startup because CUDA2 needed a `16015.55 MiB` weight buffer with only `15647 MiB` free, before KV/compute buffers, in `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cuda-heavy-extra-moe-cuda-gate-up-31-43-20260605T033336Z`.
- ROCm GPU offload of the extra-layer `ffn_gate_exps` and `ffn_up_exps` tensors is better than CPU spill but still rejected. `blk.31 -> ROCm1` and `blk.43 -> ROCm0` ran at `404.53 PP / 30.76 TG` with hash `76e17c...` in `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cuda-heavy-extra-moe-rocm-gate-up-31-43-20260605T033421Z`.
- Mixed CUDA+ROCm expert spill is also rejected. Putting `blk.31.ffn_gate_exps` on `CUDA3`, `blk.31.ffn_up_exps` on `ROCm1`, and `blk.43.ffn_gate/up_exps` on `ROCm0` ran at `403.82 PP / 29.29 TG` with hash `125a4d...` in `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cuda-heavy-extra-moe-mixed-gate-up-31-43-20260605T033540Z`.
- CUDA split-buffer offload for the extra layer MoE experts is currently blocked by backend support, not memory. `blk.31.ffn_*_exps.weight=CUDA1_Split` and `blk.43.ffn_*_exps.weight=CUDA0_Split` are rejected because CUDA split buffers do not support 3D `GGML_OP_MUL_MAT_ID` expert tensors (`split buffer override CUDA1_Split is not compatible ... op MUL_MAT_ID`). This is now a promising code-level lead because it would keep the extra-layer MoE work on NVIDIA instead of CPU.
- Moving output from CUDA3 to CUDA2 with the same `13,13,7,11,11,7` split caused CUDA OOM during `mul_mat_q`, so CUDA3 remains the best output owner.
- `GGML_CUDA_P2P=1` did not beat the best run.
- CPU router projection is too slow because CPU/GPU transfer overhead dominates.
- MiniMax MoE graph reroute to CUDA requires huge compute buffers and falls back without pipeline parallelism.
- Moving actual layer-0 MoE expert weights to CUDA1 and routing layer-0 MoE ops to CUDA1 avoided the huge compute-buffer fallback, but it still lost badly: shifted-split baseline was `456.38 PP`, while the MoE weight/ops override dropped to `379.45 PP`. This rejects a simple one-layer weight-placement disaggregation path because cross-device activation/copy overhead dominates.
- MiniMax expert activation is broad, not cold-expert dominated. The profile saw 256 experts, top-8 routing, 61 profiled layers, and most layers used roughly 125-251 experts in the prompt; the hottest expert per layer was only about 3-12% of selections. This weakens the case for simple CPU cold-expert offload.
- Experimental q4_0 direct-dequant CUDA MMA FA selected correctly on CUDA prefill shapes, but it is not a high-PP win. Earlier runs showed only a tiny same-ubatch gain (`474.28 PP` vs `473.87 PP`) and did not unlock `ub456+`. A later same-build shape-gate sweep at `ub512 --reserve-pp-outputs 1` matched the accepted output hash for all `ub512` q4-direct variants, with best diagnostic result `487.54 PP`, but this is within noise of the promoted `487.51 PP` baseline. The selector cleanup that restricts `mode=all` to actually supported direct tile shapes is safe, but also flat: hot baseline was `487.26 PP / 29.84 TG`, patched `q4direct_all` was `486.85 PP / 29.53 TG`, same accepted hash. The `ub528` q4-direct shape-gated probe still produced rejected hash `20bee41d...`, so q4 direct does not make larger ubatch production-safe.
- MMQ selector diagnostic bug: one invalid artifact (`/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-mmq-diagnostics-20260604T083632Z`) forced the default MMQ search to stop at `mmq_x=8`, producing a false `248.64 PP` control. It is marked with `INVALID_SELECTOR_BUG_MMQ_X8` and excluded.
- Disabling CUDA MMQ stream-K is not viable. The `ub448` probe ran for minutes versus a ~24 s prompt eval control and was aborted as non-competitive.
- Forcing CUDA MMQ tile width did not help. `x=96` and `x=64` were both slower at `ub448` (`473.60/473.65 PP` vs `475.53 PP`) and still failed at `ub456`.
- Disabling MMQ on CUDA3 did not help. `ub456` moved to a cuBLAS fallback allocation OOM on CUDA3, so the issue is broader CUDA3 headroom, not only MMQ tile selection.
- Current `ub456` forced-MMQ failures OOM in CUDA3 VMM allocation from vector flash-attention (`ggml_cuda_pool_vmm::alloc()` called by `launch_fattn<128,2,1>` / `ggml_cuda_flash_attn_ext_vec_case<128,q4_0,q4_0>`). CUDA3 MMQ-disable OOMs in `ggml_cuda_op_mul_mat_cublas()`.
- FA allocation diagnostics confirm the memory cliff. The accepted `ub448` control still matches the baseline hash at `475.15 PP / 31.23 TG`. At `ub456`, the uncapped vector fallback can choose vector mode with only `1.38 MiB` free and then request a `21.38 MiB` `dst_tmp` allocation. With the vector temp cap enabled, FA scratch is clamped, but the run still dies later in a tiny CUDA3 K-rotation `MUL_MAT` with the same `1.38 MiB` free. Disabling CUDA graphs does not change this failure.
- Moving one layer from CUDA3 to AMD makes `ub456` run, but it drops to `440.59 PP`, so a full-layer headroom fix loses more than the larger ubatch gains.
- Moving output to CUDA0 cannot reserve pipeline compute buffers on that 3090; moving output to CPU runs but drops to `358.14 PP / 22.07 TG`.
- A narrow `output.weight=CUDA0_Split` override does remove output-weight pressure from CUDA3, but the generic split-buffer lm-head reserves a `3881.48 MiB` CUDA0 compute buffer and forces no-pipeline fallback. This rejects generic output split-buffer placement as a production path; a custom low-scratch sharded lm-head would be needed.
- `--reserve-pp-outputs 1` confirms that over-reserving prompt-output rows contributes to startup/runtime headroom. It makes `ub456` run with the default CUDA3 output owner, but only at about `455.3 PP`; moving output to CUDA0 with the same reserve patch reaches only `456.1 PP`. The default `ub448` control remains clean at `474.96 PP / 31.20 TG` with the accepted hash, so the patch is safe and useful mainly for larger ubatch.
- The same reserve patch becomes useful at larger ubatch. `ub512` repeats cleanly with the promoted CLI at `482.03` and `487.51 PP`, with coherent output and no fallback/OOM. The earlier env-only diagnostic repeated at `487.55` and `486.26 PP`. `ub520` and `ub524` are sane but slower than `ub512`. `ub528` and `ub544` are rejected even though raw PP is high, because both start echoing the benchmark prompt text. Disabling server context checkpoints does not fix `ub528`: `--ctx-checkpoints 0` still returns the same rejected `20bee41d...` prompt-echo hash at `486.49 PP`.
- `LLAMA_SERVER_PROMPT_DEBUG=1` confirms `ub528` is not a server output-row indexing bug. The final `ub512` prompt chunk is `257` tokens and samples from `tok_idx=256`; the final `ub528` prompt chunk is `433` tokens and samples from `tok_idx=432`. Both are the correct final local rows. The deterministic `temperature=0.0` payload produces the same first two tokens (`2.`), then diverges at token 3: `ub512` emits a markdown heading, while `ub528` emits ` Benchmark` and starts prompt echo. This points to prompt-processing numerical/kernel-shape trajectory, not random sampling or wrong row selection.
- Cheap shape controls do not beat the current promoted `ub512`. Forcing `-b 528 -ub 512` avoids the prompt-echo class but drops to `433.09 PP`, so physical split stabilization is too expensive. Narrow boundary probes `ub526` and `ub527` remain coherent, but both are slower than `ub512` at `484.96 PP` and `484.40 PP`.

## Stage profile evidence

Split profiling of the then-current best command with `--profile-splits 3` showed the layer-mode bottleneck was still the AMD-owned full layers after first-ubatch setup noise:

Artifact: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-profile-splits3-20260604T043127Z`

| prompt ubatch | ROCm1 | ROCm0 | CUDA3 | CUDA1 | CUDA0 | CUDA2 |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| pp-1 | 572.328 ms | 267.796 ms | 250.986 ms | 82.749 ms | 24.590 ms | 26.751 ms |
| pp-2 | 407.760 ms | 429.366 ms | 93.507 ms | 100.432 ms | 100.050 ms | 34.874 ms |
| pp-3 | 342.164 ms | 382.905 ms | 41.455 ms | 93.824 ms | 92.684 ms | 28.509 ms |

This supports the earlier interpretation: current layer-mode PP is bottlenecked by AMD stages, but simple sub-layer MoE migration is not enough because it introduces expensive cross-device movement.

| reserve diagnostic | `LLAMA_RESERVE_PP_OUTPUTS=1`, default output, `ub544` | 496.5104 | 30.1619 | `5b712d...` | rejected: prompt echo |

Notes:

- The mixed-vendor host-staged bridge is real, but enabling it in the current layer-mode baseline does not improve PP. This indicates current layer-mode PP is not dominated by inter-stage transfer cost.
- Full mixed tensor mode is no longer blocked at graph-construction level for f16 KV when `GGML_META_MINIMAX_DISTRIBUTED_RMS_NORM=1` is enabled. It remains blocked for production Q4/Q8 KV because tensor split rejects quantized KV, and it is currently much slower than layer mode even before quantized KV work. A narrow outer-layer-mode plus CUDA split-buffer override prototype was also implemented for dense `MUL_MAT` tensors, but the current form is slower than control.
- Hybrid CUDA Meta layer-stage was implemented as an opt-in prototype: `ROCm1,ROCm0,Meta(CUDA3,CUDA1,CUDA0,CUDA2)`. It avoids AMD+NVIDIA tensor collectives and lets CUDA own up to 34 layers. f16-KV PP remains below same-payload q4 layer mode even at whole-prompt ubatch. Q4 KV is now graph-functional with the newer unsafe Meta reshape/view remaps, but production full-context cache-aware runs with fitting 32/33 CUDA-layer shapes stop at only `258.96-265.29 PP`, so the current Meta layer-stage is rejected as a high-PP path.
- q4 direct CUDA MMA FA is isolated to the `8x8` MiniMax path. It is faster but deterministically corrupts output by echoing prompt text. The `32x2` mode is not the active MiniMax path; after selector fix it falls back safely and matches baseline output.
- Changing q4 direct dequant from half multiply to float multiply did not fix correctness. Therefore the remaining q4 direct bug is likely deeper in direct K/V tile semantics, MMA layout expectations, or synchronization, not simple q4 numeric rounding.
- Splitting the q4 direct path by component did not isolate a safe production path. At `ub256` all direct component variants match baseline output, at `ub416` they produce coherent but different output, and at `ub448` the active `8x8` direct path still produces the same prompt-echo failure hash. K-only and V-only at `ub448` still OOM because the non-direct side keeps enough f16 scratch to hit CUDA3 pressure.
- The VMM unused-tail trim diagnostic did not free the failing allocation path. The `ub456` failure remains a late CUDA3 `MUL_MAT` OOM, with no useful trim events before the failure.
- The dense CUDA split-buffer prototype stayed in pipeline mode, so the slowdown is not a fallback artifact. All-layer attention split added a `CUDA0_Split` model buffer of `2766.75 MiB`, raised CUDA0 compute buffer use to `1264.32 MiB`, and produced `314` scheduler graph splits. A one-layer split added only `44.62 MiB` and `14` graph splits but still reduced PP by about 11%.
- The output-only split-buffer prototype does not stay in pipeline mode. It reduces CUDA3 persistent weight pressure, but the generic split-buffer output projection allocates too much CUDA0 compute scratch. Any future output relocation needs a custom low-scratch sharded lm-head instead of `-ot output.weight=CUDA*_Split`.
- The PP-output reservation prototype is safe when disabled and useful diagnostically. It proves a smaller reserved output graph can avoid the late `ub456` CUDA3 OOM, but the resulting `ub456` throughput is still about `20 PP` below the current best.
- `LLAMA_GRAPH_REUSE_DISABLE=1` does not expose a PP win. A naive copy-slot rotation prototype showed higher early progress but aborted due scheduler graph mutation/state accumulation (`GGML_SCHED_MAX_SPLIT_INPUTS`). A real ping-pong implementation needs non-mutating split plans or explicit per-ubatch graph/input buffers.
- Extra-layer MiniMax expert spill is rejected in all simple forms tried. CPU spill is far below baseline and not output-sane, CUDA same-vendor spill OOMs, and ROCm/mixed spill drops to about `404 PP`; a future expert path would require a new expert-aware split-buffer `MUL_MAT_ID` implementation, not tensor overrides.
- The first CUDA+RAM MoE scheduler prototype is now screened. A default-off heuristic `GGML_SCHED_MOE_FULL_COPY_RATIO` was added in [ggml-backend.cpp](/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/ggml/src/ggml-backend.cpp) so broad-coverage MoE staging can switch from fragmented expert-range copies to one bulk tensor copy. A generic `--n-cpu-moe 1` smoke was not useful because it offloads a ROCm-owned early layer and did not reach `server is listening` after about `9` minutes; artifact: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cpumoe1-fullcopydiag-20260606T224307Z`. A targeted CUDA3-owned layer test with `-ot blk\.26\.ffn_(up|gate|down)_exps\.weight=CPU` freed about `1.94 GiB` on CUDA3 and allowed `ub832` to start, but prompt processing dropped below the `300 PP` stop gate by about `22464` processed tokens and reached about `283.27 PP` at `25792` processed tokens; artifact: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-cuda3moe1-ub832-fullcopy-20260606T225324Z`. This rejects more simple static CPU-offload sweeps as a high-PP path.

## Proposal status

| proposal | status |
|---|---|
| 1. Disaggregate attention and experts | Diagnostics/probes rejected for simple MoE forms: scheduler-only MoE reroute causes huge compute buffers, and one-layer MoE weight+op movement to CUDA slows PP. An env-gated CUDA-only Meta layer-stage can now express a coarse CUDA subgroup inside layer mode. Q4 KV is graph-functional with unsafe Meta remaps, but full-context cache-aware throughput is below the `300 PP` gate. True attention/FFN disaggregation remains a major rewrite. |
| 2. Ping-pong micro-batch scheduling | Rejected for the simple scheduler forms tried. `LLAMA_PIPELINE_UNSAFE_NO_REUSE_SYNC` was flat, split-copy rotation was flat/slower, and split-copy plus graph-input copy was slower. Per-input copy detail now shows CUDA3 waits about `1.08-1.19 s` on `l_out-25` from ROCm0 while the actual dispatch is only about `4-5 ms`, so the boundary is ROCm stage completion latency, not transfer bandwidth. A real ping-pong win would need a deeper multi-ubatch execution model, not just rotating copy slots inside the current serial split loop. |
| 3. Dynamic gating/load-aware experts | Instrumented router top-k histograms. Not implemented as routing because it would change selected experts/output and current layer-mode storage does not distribute experts across CUDA/ROCm within a layer. |
| 4. Cold expert CPU offload/LRU | Profiled expert usage; broad activation makes simple cold-expert offload unlikely to help. CPU transfer probes are negative. The first scheduler-level CUDA+RAM prototype freed the right CUDA memory on a targeted layer but still fell below the `300 PP` gate, so more one-layer CPU-offload sweeps are rejected. |
| 5. Cross-device communication | CUDA P2P already exists behind `GGML_CUDA_P2P`; mixed CUDA+ROCm true P2P is not exposed by this host. The host-staged mixed-vendor bridge works but does not win in layer mode. Full mixed tensor mode now runs with f16 KV via distributed MiniMax Q/K RMS_NORM, but the best quick result is only `228.15 PP` versus `420.89 PP` for same-payload layer mode and `~488 PP` for the promoted high-context layer config. CUDA-subgroup Meta layer mode avoids cross-vendor collectives but reaches only `369.50 PP` f16 KV on the same 961-token payload. Direct mixed AMD+NVIDIA tensor mode remains rejected as a current high-PP path. |
| 6. Async allocation/pools | Existing CUDA path already uses per-stream pools and VMM. Current failures are real CUDA3 headroom/peak allocation failures, not repeated malloc overhead. |
| 7. Chunked FA/KV prefetch | Partially addressed by hybrid FA fallback, vector temp cap diagnostics, q4_0 direct MMA FA prototype, and FA allocation logging. Current evidence shows CUDA3 FA/K-rotation headroom is still the limit, and `--reserve-pp-outputs 1` provides enough reserve to run `ub512` without fallback. This is now the highest-priority high-PP code track. |
| 8. Graph placement scheduler | Implemented as `--placement-policy graph`; produces the winning split `13,13,7,11,11,7`. |
| 9. CPU-assisted gating/sampling | Router projection CPU probe rejected. Sampling offload is unlikely to affect PP materially. |

## Next high-value work

The remaining bottleneck is CUDA3 peak memory during prompt processing and AMD stage compute. The exact-hash baseline reaches `475.53 PP` at `ub448`. The current highest sane promoted-CLI PP candidate is `--reserve-pp-outputs 1 -b 512 -ub 512`, repeated at `482.03` and `487.51 PP`. The earlier env-only diagnostic repeated at `487.55` and `486.26 PP`.

Per user direction, the active plan is now narrowed further to tracks with a realistic chance of a large PP gain (`>=25%`). Lower-upside work such as small FA-cap portability cleanup, ordinary layer-split tuning, and minor memory tweaks is no longer active.

| benchmark | result | artifact | interpretation |

This proves the NVIDIA group can deliver much higher PP when the model/backend path fits CUDA cleanly; MiniMax is limited by mixed layer pipeline and MiniMax-specific backend behavior, not by a global server cap. |

The latest `ub456` evidence is specific:

1. Forced MMQ `x=96` and `x=64` fail in `ggml_cuda_pool_vmm::alloc()` called from vector flash-attention (`launch_fattn<128,2,1>` / `ggml_cuda_flash_attn_ext_vec_case<128,q4_0,q4_0>`).
2. FA allocation logging shows uncapped `ub456` can request a `21.38 MiB` vector `dst_tmp` allocation with only `1.38 MiB` free on CUDA3.
3. After vector temp capping, `ub456` still fails in a tiny CUDA3 `MUL_MAT` with only `1.38 MiB` free.
4. Disabling MMQ on CUDA3 fails in `ggml_cuda_op_mul_mat_cublas()`, so a full cuBLAS fallback is not a memory solution.
5. Disabling CUDA graphs does not solve the headroom failure.
6. At `ub448`, forced MMQ tile widths are slower than default, so MMQ tuning is not the next performance win.
7. Reducing PP-output graph reservation makes `ub512` viable and faster. Initial `ub528+` runs prompt-echoed, but the later HIP tile parallel-block cap recovers several higher ubatches.
8. Disabling server context checkpoints does not fix `ub528`; it keeps the same rejected prompt-echo hash.
9. Prompt-row diagnostics show `ub528` samples the correct final prompt row. The failure is a deterministic logits/numerical trajectory change, first visible at generated token 3.
10. Shape-control probes do not beat `ub512`: `-b 528 -ub 512` is coherent but much slower, and `ub526/527` are coherent but still below the former promoted `ub512` PP.
11. q4 direct shape gating does not fix the `ub528` output failure. It is useful diagnostic infrastructure, but the next FA path must reduce scratch or chunk work without changing the output trajectory.
12. Selective vector FA shows the `ub528` prompt-echo trajectory is strongly tied to ROCm/HIP final-chunk FA. HIP-only vector FA for the final `Q=433` prompt chunk avoids echo at `452.88 PP`, while CUDA-only final-chunk vector FA keeps the exact rejected `20bee41d...` hash. This is useful evidence but not a candidate because it remains slower than accepted `ub512`.
13. FA parallel-block diagnostics narrow the fault further and produced a real PP win: global `parallel_blocks=1` avoids the prompt-echo trajectory but hurts TG, while narrow HIP/non-full-chunk caps recover higher ubatches without decode TG loss. CUDA q4-direct FA then removes enough f16 K/V scratch to move the best benchmark result from `ub768` to `ub800`, repeating at `553.90` and `553.56 PP`. `ub832` now hits CUDA3 `mul_mat`/cuBLAS scratch OOM, so the immediate ceiling moved from FA scratch to dense/MoE matmul scratch.
14. Low-scratch CUDA3 MMQ chunking proved the exact `ub832` memory blockers but is rejected as a PP path. No-id dense chunks moved past the `2.76 MiB` attention projection staging failure, and ID/MoE token chunks reduced MoE staging from `21.96 MiB` to `1.71 MiB`. However Q4_K chunked MoE required `mmq_x=32`, and the live prompt rate collapsed to about `12.5-22.2 PP`, far below the current `ub800` result. The default-off regression check still passes at `552.97 PP`.
15. Per-input split-copy detail on the current `ub800` best shape proves the active pipeline bubble is not a mixed-vendor copy throughput problem. The largest wait is split `4/8` copying `l_out-25` from ROCm0 to CUDA3: only `9.38 MiB` is copied, dispatch takes about `4 ms`, but CUDA3 waits `1.08-1.19 s` for ROCm0 to finish producing the tensor. This pushes the next high-upside work toward multi-ubatch pipeline overlap, not another P2P/copy-bandwidth patch.
16. Split compute profiling gives a concrete upper bound for that overlap track. With `ub800`, the slowest steady prompt stage is ROCm0 at `579.1 ms`; ideal wavefront throughput is therefore about `1381 PP` before overhead. That does not prove `1000 PP` is reachable, but it is the strongest current evidence that scheduler architecture, not another layer split or P2P copy tweak, is the right high-upside target.

## Current Stage And Remaining Plan

The near-term target is no longer another bounded throughput branch. All local Stage-5 leads that were feasible to implement and benchmark within the current fork have now been screened against the real cache-aware benchmark. The remaining work, if resumed later, is deeper scheduler/backend architecture only. The older `/home/stefan/plan-cuda+8channelram.md` MoE planner work remains archived evidence for why the simpler CUDA+RAM routes were rejected, not as an active branch.

Interpretation of the expanded FA-node routing screening:

- All-CUDA FA routing is real signal, not noise: it improves cached processed PP by about `27%` versus the cache-aware baseline.
- The blocker is reserve memory, not routing correctness. The weighted route `1,4,4,1` materially reduced the failing 5070 reserve allocation from about `3270 MiB` to about `1751 MiB`.
- The older proposal-7 FA cap does not rescue this branch. Applying `GGML_CUDA_FATTN_MAX_PARALLEL_BLOCKS=1` to the weighted route left the reserve failure unchanged at the same `1750.94 MiB` CUDA3 allocation.
- The next obvious step, eliminating 5070 FA work entirely, is worse: the 3090-only schedule makes CUDA1 try to reserve about `5929.59 MiB`.
- That means the current weighted FA route is trapped between two bad memory shapes: small cards fail if they own any meaningful FA share, and the 3090s fail if they own nearly all of it.
- Making this branch reserve-clean would now require moving more whole layers back to AMD, which directly attacks the PP objective because AMD-owned layers are the known cached-turn bottleneck.
- This screens out the current FA-node routing family as a local high-PP path.

On the larger default cache-aware session, the same branch drops to turn 1 `297.50 PP` on the `34354`-token prompt and trips the `300 PP` cutoff before any cached turn is reached. So this combination is useful evidence that the leaf-only plus direct-F16 headroom is real, but the reopened narrow FA reroute is still not a promotable Stage-5 finish. | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-stage5-l2526-leafonly-directf16kq-fattn01-cuda1-ub832-cache2-med-20260608T025019Z`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-stage5-l2526-leafonly-directf16kq-fattn01-cuda1-ub832-cache2-default-20260608T025123Z` | close this reopened FA lane again. | cached-turn node profile of the best live default Stage-5 branch | profiled the first three cached-turn prompt graph executions on the best live default branch that still reflects the current headroom work: `GGML_SCHED_COPY_SLOTS_ON_ROTATE_ONLY=1`, `LLAMA_DIRECT_F16_KQ_MASK=1`, live `25,26 -> CUDA0_Split`, split `14,14,7,10,10,7`, `ub832`, `--profile-nodes 3`, `LLAMA_PROFILE_PP_SKIP=42`. Also traced the current MiniMax FA override hook in `llama_context::graph_get_cb()`. | this is the clearest architectural diagnosis so far. On the real cached turn, the dominant ROCm cost is attention, not MoE and not split-copy dispatch. Across the first profiled cached-turn graphs, ROCm1 attention totals about `1368-1401 ms` while ROCm1 MoE totals about `515-535 ms`; ROCm0 attention totals about `1384-1420 ms` while ROCm0 MoE totals about `463-479 ms`. At the per-layer level, ROCm attention chunks are about `98-102 ms` each, while ROCm MoE chunks are about `37-40 ms`. The moved CUDA0 MoE slices stay around `18-19 ms`, so more MoE-only tuning cannot plausibly close the remaining gap on the primary benchmark. Code inspection explains why the existing FA route underperforms: `--minimax-fattn-devices` in `graph_get_cb()` only reassigns tensors named `LLAMA_TENSOR_NAME_FATTN`, i.e. the flash-attention core, while the expensive surrounding attention work that shows up in the profile (`norm -> __fattn__`, plus the `kqv_out` tail and implicit Q/K/V projection path) is still built on the layer owner. That means the next meaningful Stage-5 continuation is not another narrow FA-core reroute. It is a broader attention-subgraph architecture change, likely requiring persistent CUDA-resident attention weights or another way to avoid copying large Q/K/V projection weights every graph execution. | `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-stage5-l2526-leafonly-directf16kq-ub832-ls1414710107-cache2-default-nodeprof-20260608T030035Z`, code: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/llama-context.cpp:3139`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/llama-graph.cpp:2200`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/llama-graph.cpp:2300` | this closes the remaining ambiguity about where the real cached-turn time is going. Keep Stage 5 active, but change its focus: stop screening more MoE-only or FA-core-only tweaks and move to a deeper attention-subgraph design if local work continues. |

| first exact prefix/tail split-attention pilot (`LLAMA_MINIMAX_FATTN_KV_SPLIT_EXACT=1`) | added the first real exact split-attention pilot in `llama-graph.cpp` on top of the new KV range-view helpers in `llama-kv-cache`: for selected shadow-capable MiniMax self-attention layers, prompt-phase attention can now build `kq_prefix` from the shadow KV prefix and `kq_tail` from the primary KV tail, concatenate the logits exactly, run one normal softmax over the combined logits, split the resulting attention weights back into prefix/tail views, and add `v_prefix * w_prefix + v_tail * w_tail` exactly. The branch stayed default-off behind `LLAMA_MINIMAX_FATTN_KV_SPLIT_EXACT=1` and was screened first on the same lighter large cached-turn harness used for the split-shape diagnostic (`LLAMA_DIRECT_F16_KQ_MASK=1`, `LLAMA_MINIMAX_FATTN_ROUTE_DISABLE=1`, `LLAMA_MINIMAX_FATTN_KV_SHADOW=1`, `LLAMA_MINIMAX_FATTN_KV_SPLIT_DEBUG=1`, split `14,14,7,10,10,7`, `-b 384 -ub 384`, `--minimax-fattn-devices CUDA0 --minimax-fattn-layers 25,26`). Two intermediate attempts failed before the working path: the first exact runtime version died in CUDA alloc sizing on quantized split KV views with nonzero offsets; the second died because CUDA does not support `q4_0 -> q4_0` copy for the materialized segment path. The surviving proof path therefore dequantizes split KV segments to `F32` before the exact attention math so the current backend stack can execute it at all. | this is the first **working** exact split-attention branch, but it is a correctness primitive, not a performance win. The final `F32` pilot serves and completes both real cached-turn payloads end-to-end on the recovered gfx906 launcher. Warmup turn: `10006` prompt tokens at `260.60 PP`, `96` decode tokens at `27.83 TG`. Cached follow-up: `3002` prompt tokens with `cache_n = 10013` at `213.46 PP`, `96` decode tokens at `25.29 TG`. That is materially slower than the lighter non-split shadow diagnostic baseline (`274.12 PP` warmup, `227.98 PP` cached). The result is still useful: it proves the exact prefix/tail topology is valid in this fork, and it narrows the next requirement sharply. | Stage 5A ROCm full-KV layout probe plus one-layer `q4_0` qcont proof | after the one-group GQA branch was closed, screened the ROCm-native cached-prefix fallback in two bounded steps on the real larger cached-turn payload class (`10006` warmup prompt tokens, then `3002` cached follow-up prompt tokens with `cache_n = 10013`) using the plain mixed layer path `--layer-split 14,12,7,11,11,7 --output-device CUDA3` and no shadow/GQA/split branches. Then added a stricter one-layer proof `LLAMA_STAGE5_ROCM_PREFIX_PACK_QCONT=1` that forces quantized `ggml_cont()` normalization of the full `q4_0` `K/V` tensors for layer `25` before `ggml_flash_attn_ext()`, still staying in `q4_0` and keeping flash attention active. | this is the clearest local screen of the ROCm packed-prefix fallback so far. Enabling one-layer full-KV `q4_0` qcont on layer `25` drops that to turn 1 `490.65 PP / 31.15 TG` and turn 2 `310.45 PP / 28.63 TG`. The request-time logs explain why: every live prompt chunk now performs extra quantized copies for the full late-layer KV span, growing from about `0.56 + 0.56 MiB` at `n_kv=1024` to about `6.34 + 6.34 MiB` at `n_kv=11008`, `6.78 + 6.78 MiB` at `11776`, `7.23 + 7.23 MiB` at `12544`, and `7.52 + 7.52 MiB` at `13056` for `K` plus `V`. So the graph-level proof confirms both sides of the fallback: there is a real quantized-layout problem on the ROCm late-layer path, but repacking the full KV span inside the prompt graph every chunk is already too expensive on one layer alone. | baseline layout probe: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-stage5a-rocmprefix-layoutprobe-plain1412-20260609T004925Z`; one-layer qcont proof: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/bench-results/minimax-stage5a-rocmprefix-qcont-layer25-plain1412-20260609T005140Z`; code: `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/llama-graph.cpp` | keep the ROCm cached-prefix fallback alive only in its deeper persistent form. Kill the graph-level repeated-qcont proof as a PP branch. If that deeper KV/backend work is not worth taking on locally, then Stage 5 has no cheap remaining local PP finisher and the fallback should be documented as blocked rather than iterated. |
| Stage 5A persistent ROCm packed-shadow write-only proof | after closing the graph-level repeated-`qcont` path, screened the narrowest deeper continuation of the ROCm cached-prefix fallback: allocate a same-device packed `q4_0` shadow for one selected late ROCm layer and maintain it at KV-write time, but do **not** consume it in attention yet. Added packed-shadow tensors plus packed row-index inputs in `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/llama-kv-cache.cpp`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/llama-kv-cache.h`, `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/llama-graph.cpp`, and `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/llama-graph.h`, behind `LLAMA_STAGE5_ROCM_PREFIX_PACK_WRITE=1` with `LLAMA_STAGE5_ROCM_PREFIX_PACK_LAYER=25`. The packed shadow stores one row per `(KV head, token)` on the same ROCm owner as layer `25`; request-time writes pack `k_cur/v_cur` from `[head_dim, n_head_kv, n_tokens]` into a contiguous head-major row layout and write them into the quantized shadow via `ggml_set_rows()`. Screened on the same real larger cached-turn replay as the plain baseline (`10006` warmup prompt tokens, then `3002` cached follow-up prompt tokens with `cache_n = 34449`) using the plain mixed layer path `14,12,7,11,11,7 -> CUDA3`. | this keeps the deeper ROCm fallback **alive**. Startup reserves only one extra packed shadow for layer `25`, costing `38.11 MiB` for `K` and `38.11 MiB` for `V`. On live prompt chunks, write-side maintenance stays bounded and predictable: the dominant `q=800` chunks log `packed_k_src_bytes=3276800` and `packed_v_src_bytes=3276800`, with the final short cached chunk at `q=66` dropping to `270336 + 270336` bytes. Most importantly, the write-only cost on the real cache-aware replay is small. Plain current-tree baseline on the same script reaches cached turn 2 `201.020993 PP / 15.087996 TG`; enabling the write-only packed shadow changes that to `200.190734 PP / 14.804696 TG`. That is only about a `0.41%` cached-PP drop and about a `1.88%` TG drop while maintaining the extra persistent packed state. So the cheap discriminator is positive: persistent pack maintenance itself is not the thing killing this lead.
