Feasibility screen for the remaining deep CUDA-only activation-bucket idea:

- The active `ub800` profile reports `183` `MUL_MAT_ID` ops per eval, which is about `61` MoE layers if each layer contributes the usual `gate/up/down` trio.
- The same profile reported about `115.8 GiB` of full expert weight bytes across the eval, which works out to about `1.90 GiB` of routed-expert weights per MoE layer.
- A hypothetical perfect 4-way resident expert-owner split across the four NVIDIA cards would therefore still require about `28.95 GiB` of expert weights per CUDA device if all MoE layers stayed resident there.
- That is before dense layers and KV. Current dense+KV residency is already about `22.2-22.7 GiB` on the 3090s in the best `11`-layer shape, about `20.2-20.7 GiB` even in the memory-freed `10`-layer FA-routing screen, and about `14.1-14.4 GiB` on the 5070s.
- The shard-profile data also shows the practical PP problem: in the full `ub800` chunk, every 4-way shard touched `64/64` local experts. So a RAM-staged compact-slot design would still move nearly the whole shard for every large PP microbatch.
- Conclusion: a compact-slot-only patch is not a plausible `>=25%` PP path on this exact hardware/model shape. Any surviving MoE planner design would need a more radical representation change than simple compact staging, or different hardware/model assumptions.

## Scrapped From Active Plan

These remain documented as evidence, but they are no longer active TODOs because they are low-upside or already rejected:

- CPU router/gating/sampling.
- Cold expert CPU offload/LRU.
- Simple scheduler-only CUDA+RAM MoE offload sweeps after the targeted CUDA3 `ub832` failure.
- Simple MoE reroute or one-layer MoE migration.
- Partial one-layer expert-axis tuning after the flat compact-activation-transfer smoke.
- One-layer expert-axis batched-MMQ overrides after the `298.15 PP` small-smoke result.
- One-layer expert-axis persistent q8 reuse after the `299.75 PP` small-smoke result.
- Generic layer-split sweeps.
- Generic `CUDA*_Split` output placement.
- CUDA split-buffer extra-layer `MUL_MAT_ID` placement in its current row-split form; it compiles and removes the compatibility blocker but does not produce a memory-feasible high-PP shape at `ctx=69376`.
- More MMQ tile-width tuning.
- Simple CUDA3 MMQ no-id/ID chunking for `ub832`; memory improves, but PP collapses.
- HIP final-chunk cap portability cleanup unless it is part of a larger `>=25%` PP path.
- Minor CUDA3 memory tweaks, output relocation, or lm-head work unless they enable a concrete `>=25%` PP path.
- Generated docs work unless needed for packaging.
- Repeating simple dense attention split-buffer overrides without a new batching/overlap design.
- More MiniMax FA-node CUDA routing subset/weight sweeps after the `1,4,4,1` and `0,1,1,0` reserve-feasibility screens.

## Sometime-Later Leads For External Review

These are not active two-hour tasks, but they are worth preserving for another AI or a later deeper engineering pass:

- Custom low-scratch sharded lm-head/output projection that avoids generic `CUDA*_Split` compute-buffer explosion. Current screen: output ownership is worth only about `480.82 MiB`, while one extra full 3090 layer is about `1991.67 MiB`, and the blocked `12,12,7,12,12,7` shape already misses on the non-output 3090 by about `43 MiB`. So a custom lm-head could help output placement experiments, but it does not by itself create a new `>=25%` PP path on this model/hardware.
- A more radical expert-aware CUDA split-buffer design for MiniMax 3D `MUL_MAT_ID` tensors that does not require extra CUDA layer residency or additional per-request compute buffers on already-full 3090/5070 devices. The first row-split prototype is documented as rejected above.
- CUDA-only tensor parallel inside the NVIDIA subgroup while keeping AMD devices as ordinary layer-mode stages.
- Production Q4/Q8 KV support for Meta/tensor split, including flattened and rectangular quantized `RESHAPE` split-state views.
- Host-staged collective batching for mixed AMD<->NVIDIA tensor mode: persistent pinned rings, NUMA-bound copy threads, larger transfer coalescing, and stream/event overlap.
- A true multi-ubatch pipeline executor with double-buffered graph inputs, not the rejected copy-slot rotation prototype.
- HIP final-chunk FA kernel stability audit so portable prompt lengths do not need exact `Q_MIN/Q_MAX` caps.
- q4-direct FA correctness audit for active MiniMax tile shapes, including K/V tile layout, synchronization, and direct-dequant numeric equivalence.
- Memory-residency surgery to make the `12,12,7,12,12,7` CUDA-heavy split fit, possibly by compressing or relocating only non-critical persistent tensors without CPU execution. Current screen: even if it fit, it only removes two layers from the `14`-layer ROCm1 bottleneck, so the best-case cached-turn stage-time uplift is only about `14/12 = 1.167x` before new overheads; that is below the current `>=25%` active-work bar.
- Vulkan dma-buf or EGL/NvSciBuf interop only if new driver evidence shows AMD Vulkan memory can be imported into CUDA; the previous OPAQUE_FD AMD->CUDA test failed.
- UCX/RDMA or peer-memory paths only if new hardware/driver support appears; no usable RDMA path was detected on this host.
- Model-specific graph placement with per-op measured costs after new kernels land, rather than more ordinary layer-split sweeps.

## Stage 5A Update

Current active throughput stage remains `Stage 5`.
All earlier throughput stages are done or screened out.
`Stage 6` remains report / handoff upkeep only.

The near-term implementation target is now explicitly narrowed:

- `Stage 5A`: native exact prefix/tail split attention
- `Stage 5B`: fallback only, not an immediate build target

The updated `Stage 5A` rule set is:

- do not continue the current `F32` KV materialization proof path as a performance design
- do not reopen callback-level reroutes, simple KV-local variants, or owner-override churn
- do not start `Stage 5B` until `Stage 5A` is either proven non-viable or clearly insufficient

### Stage 5A Goal

Stage 5A now has to be read more narrowly and more usefully:

- keep the exact prefix/tail split path as a correctness primitive
- but treat the real objective as `native prompt-time attention compute rebalancing without long-span F32 KV materialization`

So two leads are still allowed inside the same stage:

1. native exact split attention that genuinely avoids long-span `F32` K/V materialization
2. prompt-time attention compute rebalance that moves a meaningful share of late-layer long-context work off ROCm

The exact prefix/tail topology is still valid engineering work, but it is no longer assumed to be the only plausible Stage-5A performance design. Prefix immutability does **not** eliminate attention work for new queries; it only changes residency and layout constraints.

### Stage 5A Native Exact-Split Goal

Replace the current exact prefix/tail split-attention proof path with a native lower-overhead partial-attention / reduction path that:

- keeps K/V resident and quantized where they already live
- avoids generic `ggml_copy` of long K/V spans into `F16` or `F32` temporaries
- computes local partial attention per KV domain
- reduces only compact partial results plus softmax statistics
- preserves exact softmax correctness
- keeps decode conservative unless prompt gains are proven

The exact reducer semantics must be:

- per domain `d`, compute:
  - `partial_max = m_d`
  - `partial_sumexp = l_d`
  - `partial_num = u_d = sum_j exp(score_j - m_d) * V_j`
- exact global combine:
  - `m = max_d(m_d)`
  - `L = sum_d exp(m_d - m) * l_d`
  - `U = sum_d exp(m_d - m) * u_d`
  - `final_output = U / L`

Use `partial_num`, not an ambiguous normalized partial output.

### Stage 5A.0 Instrumentation

Before replacing the proof path, add precise logging for:

- `f32_kv_materialized_bytes`
- `f16_kv_materialized_bytes`
- `quantized_kv_view_bytes`
- `q_broadcast_bytes`
- `partial_num_bytes`
- `partial_stats_bytes`
- `cross_domain_transfer_bytes`
- selected split layers
- detected phase: prompt/prefill/cache-continuation/decode
- `n_q`
- `n_kv`
- Q shape
- K/V shape
- K/V ggml type
- K/V owner device
- Q owner device
- reducer device
- output owner device
- fallback count and fallback reason
- allocator reserve sizes
- graph reuse count
- per-device attention time where available

Hard rule:

- if `f32_kv_materialized_bytes != 0` in the native path, the run is not a valid `Stage 5A` success

### Stage 5A.1 Same-Device Exact Split Reducer

Before mixed AMD/CUDA work, validate exact reducer correctness on one device first.

Goal:

- split one attention operation into two KV spans on the same backend/device
- compute `partial_max`, `partial_sumexp`, and `partial_num`
- reduce them exactly
- compare against the unsplit baseline

Continue only if:

- correctness matches within expected FA/quant tolerance
- no `F32` K/V materialization
- no CPU fallback
- no graph instability
- same-device split overhead stays bounded

Kill or fix before mixed-domain work if:

- reducer math is wrong
- same-device split is already too slow
- K/V silently materializes as `F32`
- allocator behavior regresses

### Stage 5A.2 Native Quantized KV Span Descriptor

Use a native KV span descriptor rather than copy/materialized split tensors.

Suggested shape:

```c
struct kv_span {
    ggml_tensor * k_base;
    ggml_tensor * v_base;
    int64_t token_start;
    int64_t token_count;
    ggml_type k_type;
    ggml_type v_type;
    int device;
    int alignment;
    bool is_quantized;
    bool allows_tile_dequant;
};
```

Rules:

- split boundaries should align to quant blocks / tiles where possible
- do not create full `F16` / `F32` K/V tensors
- if dequantization is needed, do it inside the tile/kernel path
- any edge fallback must be small and logged
- full-span fallback is not acceptable

### Stage 5A.3 Mixed-Domain Native Partial Attention

After same-device correctness is proven, enable mixed-domain split with:

- prompt phase only
- selected layers only
- `n_q >= 256`
- `n_kv >= 8192`
- target the known dominant `q ~= 832` shape first
- decode / `n_q == 1` stays on the conservative existing path

Allowed cross-domain movement:

- Q broadcast if needed
- `partial_num`
- `partial_max`
- `partial_sumexp`
- final reduced output if needed

Not allowed:

- full K/V migration
- `F32` K/V materialization
- full K/V split-copy to another backend

Reducer owner should default to the device that minimizes the next activation transfer.

Current exact status in local code:

- mixed-domain native split **is now attempted** when `LLAMA_STAGE5_SPLIT_FORBID_F32_KV=1`
- the old graph-policy blocker is gone:
  - `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/llama-graph.cpp` now allows `use_native_kv_views = forbid_f32_kv`
- the first mixed-domain no-`F32` attempt then exposed a new quantized-layout blocker:
  - CUDA aborted in `ggml_backend_cuda_buffer_type_get_alloc_size()` on
    - `GGML_ASSERT(tensor->nb[0] == ggml_element_size(tensor))`
- the current bounded workaround is:
  - local quantized `ggml_cont()` normalization after the `permute` step for split `K/V`
  - still `q4_0`, still no long-span `F32` KV materialization
- that workaround now lets the mixed-domain native proof run end-to-end on the small harness, but only at about `96.26 PP`

That means the next exact-split continuation is no longer “make it run at all.” It is “decide whether this class has any believable scaling path on real cached-turn shapes, or pivot to GQA-group rebalance.”

### Stage 5A.3a GQA-Group Prompt-Time Compute Rebalance

This is the best new Stage-5A lead if token-domain exact split remains flat or too fragile.

Why it is structurally feasible in the current MiniMax code:

- `/home/stefan/llama.cpp-gfx906/src/models/minimax-m2.cpp` already reshapes:
  - `Qcur` to `[n_embd_head, n_head, n_tokens]`
  - `Kcur` to `[n_embd_head, n_head_kv, n_tokens]`
  - `Vcur` to `[n_embd_head, n_head_kv, n_tokens]`
- the model/hparams layer already exposes:
  - `n_head`
  - `n_head_kv`
  - `n_gqa`
  - `n_embd_k_gqa`
  - `n_embd_v_gqa`
- `wo` is applied after attention output is reassembled, so a first prototype can concatenate selected head-group outputs back on the current layer owner and leave the output projection unchanged

Prototype shape:

- selected late layers only
- prompt/cache-follow-up only
- decode unchanged
- AMD keeps primary KV ownership for decode
- CUDA gets selective `q4_0` shadow only for chosen KV-head groups
- selected GQA groups compute full-span attention on CUDA
- remaining groups compute on ROCm
- gather the head-group outputs back to the current layer owner
- run one normal `wo` there in the first prototype

Why this is better than a pure token-prefix split bet:

- it attacks compute ownership directly instead of only token-span layout
- it avoids exact cross-token softmax merge across prefix/tail spans
- it has a believable path to reducing real ROCm long-context attention time
- it fits the existing MiniMax head/group tensor shapes better than arbitrary per-head slicing

Known blockers before implementation:

- current shadow-KV path mirrors whole selected layers, not selected KV-head groups
- current `build_attn()` path consumes whole K/V tensors, not per-group domain plans
- current logging/plan metadata is layer-level, not GQA-group-level

Current local status:

- the first same-device GQA proof now exists under:
  - `LLAMA_STAGE5_GQA_SPLIT_SAME_DEVICE=1`
  - `LLAMA_STAGE5_GQA_SPLIT_LAYER=25`
  - `LLAMA_STAGE5_GQA_GROUP_BEGIN=0`
  - `LLAMA_STAGE5_GQA_GROUP_COUNT=1`
  - `LLAMA_STAGE5_GQA_SPLIT_LOG=1`
- it serves the larger small cached-style request end-to-end:
  - `8243` prompt tokens at `93.72 PP`
  - `8` decode tokens at `29.44 TG`
  - `231` graph reuses
- that is a **structural proof**, not a speed win
- the first mixed-domain one-group GQA proof also now exists under:
  - `LLAMA_STAGE5_GQA_SPLIT_MIXED_DOMAIN=1`
  - same layer/group envs as above
- it also serves end-to-end:
  - `8243` prompt tokens at `93.45 PP`
  - `8` decode tokens at `29.56 TG`
  - `231` graph reuses
- that confirms the mixed-domain ownership split is expressible in the current graph
- but it is still only a **structural proof**, not a speed win
- so the next GQA continuation should not be “optimize one-group small-proof GQA”
- the next GQA continuation should be one of:
  - stronger GQA discriminator:
    - move a meaningfully larger fraction of attention work
    - or add per-layer attention timing on a real cached-turn payload
  - otherwise the ROCm-native packed-prefix fallback

Smallest useful prototype:

- one selected late layer
- one or two KV-head groups only
- prompt phase only
- larger cached follow-up payload, not the tiny smoke
- compare:
  - baseline ROCm-owned attention
  - existing exact-split proof path
  - any surviving same-device native path
  - new GQA-group split prototype

Kill criteria:

- shadow-write or gather overhead consumes the gain
- repeated reserve/VRAM failures return
- selected-layer ROCm attention time does not drop materially
- cached-turn PP stays in the same class

### Stage 5A.4 Prompt Guard And Decode Protection

Initial split gate:

```text
use_split =
    phase_is_prompt_or_prefill_or_cache_continuation &&
    n_q >= 256 &&
    n_kv >= 8192 &&
    layer in selected_stage5_split_layers
```

Explicitly disable for:

- `n_q == 1`
- decode phase
- small prompt chunks
- unknown shapes
- untested layers

Continue only if:

- PP improves
- TG remains within about `5-10%` of baseline
- decode latency jitter does not regress materially

### Stage 5A.5 First-Class Attention Domain Plan

Add a central plan structure so ownership does not remain scattered across callbacks, runtime overrides, allocator assumptions, and KV placement.

Suggested shape:

```c
struct attention_domain_plan {
    int layer;
    phase_t phase;

    device_id q_owner;
    device_id reducer_owner;
    device_id output_owner;
    device_id next_op_owner;

    vector<kv_span_domain> kv_domains;

    bool use_split_partial;
    bool use_cuda_shadow;
    bool use_decode_fast_path;

    size_t reserved_q_bytes;
    size_t reserved_partial_num_bytes;
    size_t reserved_partial_stats_bytes;
    size_t reserved_scratch_bytes;
};
```

This should become the single source of truth for:

- prompt/decode behavior
- KV span ownership
- Q movement
- partial computation owner
- reducer owner
- output owner
- scratch reservation
- fallback rules
- logging

### Stage 5B Fallback

Only move to `Stage 5B` if `Stage 5A` native split attention is not viable or not sufficient.

`Stage 5B` is:

- persistent multi-domain attention ownership / executor
- optional selective CUDA prompt-KV shadow
- no per-turn or per-phase KV migration
- no `F16` / `F32` full KV shadow

`Stage 5B` is explicitly fallback, not a near-term build target.

### Validation Order

1. Correctness micro-test
   - split off vs split on
   - same seed / same prompt
   - require:
     - `f32_kv_materialized_bytes = 0`
     - no CPU fallback
     - no unexpected full-span fallback

2. Same-device split fixture
   - one device
   - two local KV spans
   - exact reducer

3. Exact Stage-5 controlled fixture
   - diagnostic only, not the promotion metric

4. Medium taste run
   - if turn 2 lands back near `272-273 PP`, treat it as likely dead or misrouted

5. Real large default cache-aware benchmark
   - this is the promotion metric
   - accept only if the run is stably above `300 PP`

### Kill / Continue Matrix

Continue `Stage 5A` if:

- native split beats the current `F32` proof path on the same shapes
- `f32_kv_materialized_bytes` stays zero
- partial transfer bytes are much smaller than K/V materialization bytes
- correctness stays within tolerance
- no CPU fallback
- no allocator fallback
- no split-buffer init failure
- medium taste escapes the `272-273 PP` dead class
- real benchmark moves toward or above `300 PP`

Kill or narrow `Stage 5A` if:

- `F32` K/V materialization remains
- same-device split is already too slow
- mixed split transfer overhead dominates
- reducer synchronization dominates
- graph reuse drops materially
- TG regresses badly
- real default benchmark remains below `300 PP` with no believable scaling path

### Next Implementation Prompt

Next local implementation target:

- treat local `Stage 5` work as wrapped for this cycle
- do not reopen one-group GQA, token-domain exact split as the main PP path, graph-level repeated `q4_0` repacks, write-only packed-shadow proofs, graph-level packed-shadow read proofs, or the bounded shared owner-plan runtime path
- finish `Stage 6` only:
  - keep the report and external prompt aligned with the corrected final evidence
  - preserve the benchmark artifacts and exact branch verdicts
  - state clearly that no bounded local branch crossed the real `>300 PP` cache-aware gate
- only resume throughput work later if taking on deeper scheduler/backend architecture as a separate multi-day effort
